{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_012wfVEtLyk2dEPmYNfgA7KS","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now I have a good understanding of the code. Let me trace through what happens during resharding:\n\n1. `updateShardsLoop()` runs on a periodic ticker (line 1062)\n2. It calculates desired shards (line 1065)\n3. If resharding is needed, it sends to reshardChan with a select default (line 1072)\n4. If reshardChan is busy, it logs \"Currently resharding, skipping\"\n\nThe issue is in the reshardLoop:\n1. It receives numShards from reshardChan\n2. Calls `t.shards.stop()` - flushes all pending samples from old shards\n3. Calls `t.shards.start(numShards)` - starts new shards\n\nThe race condition occurs at line 1241:\n```go\ns.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)  // RESET TO ZERO!\n```\n\nNow let me think about the specific scenario that would cause stalled shards:\n\nTimeline:\n1. Prometheus has 4 shards with some pending samples\n2. Target discovery adds new targets\n3. updateShardsLoop calculates it needs 6 shards\n4. Sends reshardChan <- 6\n5. reshardLoop receives it and calls stop()\n6. stop() closes softShutdown and calls FlushAndShutdown on all 4 old queues\n7. Some samples are flushed successfully, others are sent to the remote server\n8. But what if during the flush, the metrics are not properly decremented?\n\nWait, let me look at line 1689 again - the sample decrement happens in updateMetrics() which is called after a send attempt. But here's the issue:\n\nLooking at the sendSamplesWithBackoff function and the updateMetrics call - the samples are decremented AFTER they're sent. So:\n\n1. Once stop() acquires the write lock, it blocks any further enqueue operations while flushing all queues. Append calls that were waiting for the read lock will then encounter the closed softShutdown channel and fail, causing samples to back off and retry. After the flush deadline passes, hardShutdown is invoked, and once stop() releases the write lock, start() begins initialization.\n\nWhen start() runs, it resets pendingSamples to 0 and creates fresh queues with new shard goroutines. The backed-off samples get appended to these new shards, but since the counter was zeroed out, they're never properly accounted for. The softShutdown mechanism in enqueue() immediately returns false when the channel closes, preventing the sample from being queued and triggering a retry from the caller. It acquires the write lock at line 1281 and doesn't release it until the function returns at line 1282 (via defer).\n\nBut while holding the write lock, it:\n1. Samples are stuck somewhere - not being sent\n2. After flushDeadline (line 1289), if s.done hasn't been signaled, stop() calls hardShutdown() (line 1293)\n\n\n6. This cancels the hardShutdownCtx, which causes runShard's ctx.Done() to fire\n7. runShard drops all remaining samples and decrements the counters\n8. s.done is closed\n9. stop() returns\n10. start() is called\n\nThe critical race: what if pendingSamples isn't zero when start() gets called? If some samples were sent and decremented but others were still in flight, start() would reset the counter to zero at line 1241 anyway. However, this shouldn't occur because by the time start() executes, all goroutines should have finished and the counter should reflect the true state.\n\nThere's a potential race between line 1241 resetting pendingSamples and a runShard goroutine from the old shards still running and calling updateMetrics. Looking at reshardLoop more carefully, when stop() completes and start() is invoked, there could be a window where a runShard goroutine is still shutting down and attempting to update metrics simultaneously with the reset operation.\n\nThe key issue is that each shard set gets its own hardShutdownCtx created at line 1252, so the old and new contexts are completely separate. When stop() cancels the old context and start() creates a fresh one with new channels, there's still a timing gap where the old goroutine might be in the middle of its final updateMetrics call while the new shards are already running and modifying the same pendingSamples metric.\n\nLooking at reshardLoop more carefully, I see the real problem: between the stop() call at line 1193 and start() at line 1194, there's a window where in-flight samples from the old shards haven't finished being processed, but start() immediately resets pendingSamples to 0 at line 1241. This means any samples that were queued in the old shard but haven't been counted yet will be lost from the metric.\n\nThe WAL watcher would eventually re-send those samples and increment the counter, but the initial reset creates a gap where the counter doesn't accurately reflect what's happening. The issue compounds because stop() performs a hard shutdown after the flush deadline, potentially dropping samples that were in-flight, yet the counter gets zeroed out as if everything was cleanly accounted for.\n\nWhen start() is called again, it unconditionally resets pendingSamples to 0, but if there are samples still queued in the WAL waiting to be re-sent, those will increment the counter once the watcher processes them. It keeps retrying to enqueue samples in a loop. During resharding, when enqueue() returns false (because softShutdown is closed), it will backoff and retry.\n\nNow I have enough information to write the investigation report. The core issue is:\n\n1. When resharding is triggered, stop() is called which closes the old shards\n2. stop() waits for all old shards to flush their queues up to flushDeadline\n3. If it times out, it hard-shuts down\n4. Samples that were dropped during hard shutdown have their counters decremented\n5. Then start() is called\n6. start() calls `pendingSamples.Set(0)` which UNCONDITIONALLY RESETS the counter to zero\n\nThe race condition occurs when:\n- Samples from the WAL or Append() are in flight during resharding\n- Some samples are successfully sent and decremented\n- Some samples are dropped and decremented\n- But due to timing, new samples might have been appended after the old shards are stopped but before the new shards start\n- Or, samples that are in queues during the hard shutdown might not have their counters properly tracked\n- When start() unconditionally resets the counter to 0, it loses the count of any samples that:\n  - Were successfully sent (counter was decremented)\n  - Were dropped during hard shutdown (counter was decremented)\n  - But new samples were queued in the meantime\n\nActually, I think the real issue is simpler:\n- During stop(), if a hard shutdown occurs, samples are dropped and `pendingSamples.Sub()` is called\n- But this happens while the old shards are still closing\n- New samples might be appended at the same time (in the Append() retry loop)\n- These new samples go to the new shards (after they start)\n- But if there's a race, the This occurs specifically when the `shards.start()` function resets the metric counter without accounting for samples still in flight or queued from concurrent append operations during the resharding transition.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**Location:** `/workspace/storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1241` in the `shards.start()` function\n\n**Mechanism:**\n```go\nfunc (s *shards) start(n int) {\n    s.mtx.Lock()\n    defer s.mtx.Unlock()\n\n    s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)  // ← LINE 1241: UNCONDITIONAL RESET\n    s.qm.metrics.numShards.Set(float64(n))\n\n    newQueues := make([]*queue, n)\n    // ... create new shards ...\n}\n```\n\nThe `pendingSamples` metric is unconditionally reset to zero when starting new shards, without accounting for samples that may:\n- Still be in-flight from old shards during the flush-to-completion phase\n- Be queued in the old shard queues during hard shutdown\n- Be pending in the WAL for re-transmission\n- Have been appended during the resharding window but not yet confirmed sent\n\n## Race Condition Timeline\n\n1. **T0:** `updateShardsLoop()` detects need for resharding (e.g., 4→6 shards)\n   - Sends `reshardChan <- numShards` (line 1072)\n   - Logs: \"Remote storage resharding from=4 to=6\"\n\n2. **T1:** `reshardLoop()` receives signal and calls `stop()`\n   - `stop()` closes `softShutdown` channel (RLock held) (line 1275)\n   - Acquires write lock (line 1281)\n   - Calls `FlushAndShutdown()` on all queues (line 1284)\n\n3. **T2:** Old shard goroutines (`runShard()`) begin flushing\n   - Send final batches via `sendSamples()`\n   - Call `updateMetrics()` which decrements `pendingSamples.Sub()` (line 1689)\n   - *Meanwhile:* Concurrent `Append()` calls that hit closed `softShutdown` retry with backoff (exponential backoff, loop at line 745)\n\n4. **T3:** If `flushDeadline` times out (default 1 minute, line 1289):\n   - `hardShutdown()` is called (line 1293)\n   - Context cancelled, `runShard()` drops remaining samples\n   - Drops are counted: `pendingSamples.Sub(float64(droppedSamples))` (line 1569)\n\n5. **T4:** `reshardLoop()` continues and calls `start(numShards)`\n   - **CRITICAL:** Line 1241 executes: `pendingSamples.Set(0)`\n   - This unconditional reset loses count of any in-flight operations\n\n6. **T5:** New shards start and receive backed-off append samples\n   - Backed-off samples from T2-T4 finally enqueue\n   - New queues process these samples\n   - BUT: Any samples that should have been tracked during the transition are now lost\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Code References\n\n**Primary Issue - Unconditional Reset:**\n- File: `/workspace/storage/remote/queue_manager.go`\n- Line 1241: `s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)` in `shards.start()`\n- Lines 1237-1266: Full `start()` function\n\n**Stop Function - Where Tracking is Lost:**\n- Line 1281-1282: Write lock held during flush wait\n- Line 1284: `FlushAndShutdown()` called in new goroutines (may not complete)\n- Line 1289: `flushDeadline` timeout triggers hard shutdown\n- Line 1569: Hard shutdown drops samples and decrements counter\n\n**Reshard Trigger:**\n- Line 1189: `reshardLoop()` receives reshard signal\n- Line 1193-1194: Sequential `stop()` then `start()` calls (no error checking)\n- Line 1072-1074: `updateShardsLoop()` sends reshard with select default (skips if busy)\n\n**Sample Append During Resharding:**\n- Lines 702-758: `Append()` function retries indefinitely with backoff\n- Line 745: `continue outer` on enqueue failure (retry loop)\n- Samples retry with exponential backoff during resharding window\n\n### Test Evidence\n\n**Existing Tests That Could Expose This:**\n- `/workspace/storage/remote/queue_manager_test.go:514` - `TestReshard()`\n  - Manually calls `m.shards.stop()` and `m.shards.start(i)`\n  - No assertion on pending sample tracking across reshards\n\n- `/workspace/storage/remote/queue_manager_test.go:592` - `TestReshardPartialBatch()`\n  - Rapid reshard cycles during concurrent append operations\n  - Specifically designed to test for deadlocks, not metric consistency\n\n## Affected Components\n\n### Primary Packages\n- `storage/remote` - Queue manager and shard orchestration\n- `storage/remote/queue_manager.go` - Core resharding logic\n\n### Metrics Affected\n- `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` - **PRIMARY**: Incremented on enqueue (line 1326), decremented on send (line 1689) or hard drop (line 1569), but reset to 0 on shard restart\n- `prometheus_remote_storage_exemplars_pending` - Same issue (line 1242)\n- `prometheus_remote_storage_histograms_pending` - Same issue (line 1242)\n\n### Affected Flows\n1. **Normal Send Path:** Sample → Enqueue (pending++) → Send (pending--) → Success\n   - Works during normal operation\n\n2. **Hard Shutdown Path:** Sample → Enqueue (pending++) → ctx.Done() → Drop (pending--) → Close\n   - Works, but counter gets reset if new shard starts immediately after\n\n3. **Reshard + Concurrent Append Path:**\n   - Sample enqueued to old shard (pending++)\n   - Reshard triggered, `stop()` closes softShutdown\n   - Sample retry hits backoff\n   - `start()` resets pending to 0\n   - Sample finally enqueues to new shard (pending++, but counter was reset)\n   - **BROKEN**: Counter tracking is now inconsistent\n\n## Why It's Intermittent\n\nThe issue is intermittent because it depends on precise timing alignment:\n\n1. **Timing Window:** The race only manifests when samples are appended during the ~millisecond window between:\n   - Old shards closing (`stop()` completes)\n   - New shards starting (`start()` resets counter)\n\n2. **Backoff Variability:** Append retry backoff is exponential (starts at 5ms, doubles each retry):\n   - Sometimes retries succeed before shard stop completes\n   - Sometimes retries are still pending when new shards start\n\n3. **Workload Dependency:**\n   - High-frequency targets → More concurrent appends → Higher probability\n   - Low-frequency targets → Fewer in-flight samples → Race is unlikely\n   - Reshard frequency affects window size\n\n4. **Flush Timeout Path:**\n   - If `flushDeadline` is exceeded and hard shutdown occurs, samples are dropped and counter decremented\n   - Immediate `start()` call resets counter → Lost information\n   - If flush completes cleanly, counter is already accurate before reset\n\n## Recommended Diagnostics\n\n### Metrics to Monitor\n1. `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` - Watch for:\n   - Sudden reset to 0 after non-zero value\n   - Stuck at non-zero for extended periods (no send progress)\n   - Comparison with `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_total` (should match)\n\n2. `prometheus_remote_storage_shards` - Monitor:\n   - Value changes (indicates resharding)\n   - Correlation with pending samples anomalies\n\n3. `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_dropped_total` - Check for:\n   - Drops during resharding events\n   - Unaccounted dropped samples\n\n### Logs to Review\n1. \"Remote storage resharding from=X to=Y\" - Reshard triggered\n2. \"Currently resharding, skipping.\" - Reshard already in progress (select default hit)\n3. \"Failed to flush all samples on shutdown\" - Hard shutdown occurred\n4. \"Resharding queues\" / \"Resharding done\" - If logged separately\n\n### Debugging Steps\n1. Enable verbose logging in `updateShardsLoop()` and `reshardLoop()`\n2. Add timestamp markers around `pendingSamples.Set(0)` in `start()`\n3. Track sample lifecycle: when enqueued, when decremented, when reset\n4. Compare pending counter with actual queue depths before/after reshard\n5. Profile goroutine count during resharding to detect leaks or races\n\n## Recommendation\n\n**Fix Strategy:**\n\nInstead of unconditionally resetting `pendingSamples` in `start()`, the metric should:\n\n1. **Preserve the count** if samples are still pending during shard transition\n2. **Track samples through resharding** by:\n   - Recording the pending count before `stop()`\n   - Ensuring all samples from old shards are either sent or dropped (counter decremented)\n   - Starting new shards without resetting the counter\n   - Only resetting counter if it reaches zero naturally\n\n**Alternative Approaches:**\n- Move `pendingSamples.Set(0)` to happen only when counter is naturally zero\n- Recalculate pending from sum of all queue depths instead of tracking incrementally\n- Add synchronization barrier to ensure no samples in-flight during counter reset\n- Use atomic compare-and-swap to only reset if counter hasn't changed since stop()\n\n**Testing Additions:**\n- Add assertion in `TestReshardPartialBatch` to verify pending samples consistency before/after reshard\n- Add test that validates pending counter matches actual queue depths\n- Stress test with rapid resharding and high-frequency appends\n\n## Related Code Sections\n\nThe issue is fundamentally a synchronization problem between:\n- Metric counter lifecycle (incremented on enqueue, decremented on send/drop)\n- Shard lifecycle (old shards stop, new shards start)\n- Concurrent operations (appends, sends, retries all happening in parallel)\n\nThe `softShutdown` channel pattern correctly prevents new enqueues, but the unconditional `Set(0)` assumes no pending samples exist, which is not guaranteed due to backoff-retry loops and in-flight requests.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":5,"cache_creation_input_tokens":4832,"cache_read_input_tokens":53603,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":4832},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"6128b09a-1fd1-4ab3-9a81-1bbe6124f333","uuid":"78276896-5dd7-4d64-b027-951125c67fb6"}

Profile goroutine count during resharding to detect leaks or races\n\n## Recommendation\n\n**Fix Strategy:**\n\nInstead of unconditionally resetting `pendingSamples` in `start()`, the metric should:\n\n1. **Preserve the count** if samples are still pending during shard transition\n2. **Track samples through resharding** by:\n   - Recording the pending count before `stop()`\n   - Ensuring all samples from old shards are either sent or dropped (counter decremented)\n   - Starting new shards without resetting the counter\n   - Only resetting counter if it reaches zero naturally\n\n**Alternative Approaches:**\n- Move `pendingSamples.Set(0)` to happen only when counter is naturally zero\n- Recalculate pending from sum of all queue depths instead of tracking incrementally\n- Add synchronization barrier to ensure no samples in-flight during counter reset\n- Use atomic compare-and-swap to only reset if counter hasn't changed since stop()\n\n**Testing Additions:**\n- Add assertion in `TestReshardPartialBatch` to verify pending samples consistency before/after reshard\n- Add test that validates pending counter matches actual queue depths\n- Stress test with rapid resharding and high-frequency appends\n\n## Related Code Sections\n\nThe issue is fundamentally a synchronization problem between:\n- Metric counter lifecycle (incremented on enqueue, decremented on send/drop)\n- Shard lifecycle (old shards stop, new shards start)\n- Concurrent operations (appends, sends, retries all happening in parallel)\n\nThe `softShutdown` channel pattern correctly prevents new enqueues, but the unconditional `Set(0)` assumes no pending samples exist, which is not guaranteed due to backoff-retry loops and in-flight requests.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
